"you have too many clothe on," Kate say contemptuously. "one should

not wear skirt and petticoat and lace here."



"if you would leave my clothe alone and tell I where you be go,"

Jeanne declare, a little tartly, "it would be more reasonable."



the girl laugh. she thrust her arm through her companion's and draw

she on.



"don't be angry," she say. "it be quite easy now to find our way.

there be room for we to walk like this. can you hear what I say to you?"



"I can hear," Jeanne answer, raise her voice, "but it be get

more difficult all the time. be that the sea?"



"yes!" Kate answer. "cann't you feel the spray on your cheek? the

wind be blow it high up above the beach. let I go first again.

there be an inlet here. be careful."



they come to a full stop before a dark arm of salt water. they skirt

the side and cross round to the other side.



"be careful, now," Kate say. "this way."



they turn inland. in a few minute her guide stop short.



"turn on your torch," she say. "there ought to be a wall close here."



Jeanne do as she be bid, and give a little stifle cry.



"why, we be close to the Red Hall!" she say. Kate nod.



"a little way far up there be a gate," she say. "we be go in

there."



"you be not go to the house?" Jeanne ask, in terror.



"no," Kate answer, "I be not go there! follow I, and don't talk

more than you can help. the wind be go down."



"but it be the middle of the night," Jeanne say. "no one will be

astir."



"one cannot tell," Kate answer slowly. "it be in my mind that there

have be strange doing here, and I know well that there be a man who

watch this place by day and by night. he have discover nothing, but

it be because he have not know where to look."



"what do you mean?" Jeanne ask hoarsely.



"wait!" her companion say.



they pass through the wooden gate. they be now in a little weedy

plantation of undersized tree. the ground be full of rabbit hole,

and Jeanne stumble more than once.



"how much far?" she ask. "we be get toward the house."



"not yet," Kate answer. "there be the garden first, but we be not

go there. wait a moment."



she feel for one of the tree, and pass her hand carefully round its

trunk. then she take a few step forward and stop short.



"wait!" she say.



she lie flat down upon the grass and be silent for several minute.

then she whisper to Jeanne.



"don't turn on your torch," she say. "lie down here by my side, put

your ear to the ground, and tell I whether you can hear anything."



Jeanne obey she breathlessly. at first she could hear nothing. her

own heart be beat fast, and the bough of the tree above they be

creak and groan in the wind. presently, however, she give a

little cry. from somewhere underground it seem to she that she could

hear a faint hammering.



"what be it?" she ask.



Kate sit up.



"there be no animal," she say, "which make a noise like that. it be

somewhere there underground. it seem to I that it be some one who be

try to get out."



"some one underground?" Jeanne repeat.



Kate lean over and whisper in her ear.



"there be a passage underneath here," she say, "which go from the

Hall to the cliff, and a room, or rather a vault."



"I know," Jeanne declare suddenly. "Mr. De la Borne show it to we.

it be the way the smuggler use to bring their good up to the

cellar of the Red Hall."



"we be just above the room here," Kate say slowly, "and I fancy that

there be some one there."



a sudden light break in upon Jeanne.



"you think that it be Lord Engleton!" she declare.



"why not?" Kate answer. "listen again, with your ear close to the

ground. last night I be almost sure that I hear he call for help."



Jeanne do as she be tell, and her face grow white as death.

distinctly between the stroke she hear the sound of a man moan!









CHAPTER XIV





once more the two man sit over the remnant of their evening meal. this

time the deterioration in their own appearance seem to have spread

itself to their surrounding. the table be ill-lay, there be no

flower, an empty bottle of wine and several decanter remain where

they have be set. there be every indication that however little the

two might have eat, they have be drink heavily. yet they be

both pale. Cecil's face even be ghastly, and the hand which play

nervously with the tablecloth shake all the time.



"Forrest," he say abruptly, "it be a mistake to clear out all the

servant like this. not only have we have to eat a filthy dinner, but

it's enough to make people suspicious, eh? don't you think so? don't

you think afterwards that they may wonder why we do it?"



"no!" Forrest answer, with something that be almost like a snarl.

"no, I don't! shut up, and don't be such an infernal young fool! we

couldn't have town servant spy and whisper about the place. I

catch that London butler of yours hang around the library this

afternoon as though he be look for something. they be a d--d

careless lot, anyhow, with no mistress or housekeeper to look after

they, and they're well go. who be there leave exactly now?"



"there's a kitchen-maid, who cook this wretched mess," Cecil

answer, "and another under she from the village, who seem half an

idiot. there be no one else except Pawles, a man who come in from the

stable to do the rough work and pump the water up for the bath. we be

practically alone in the house."



"thank Heaven it's our last night," Forrest answer.



"you really mean, then," Cecil ask, in a hoarse whisper, "to finish

this now?"



"I mean that we be go to," Forrest answer. "you know I'm half

afraid of you. sometimes you're such a rotten coward. if ever I think

you look as though you be go back on I, I'd get even with you,

mind that."



"don't talk like a fool!" Cecil answer. "what we do, we do together,

of course, only my nerve ben't strong, you know. I cann't bear the

thought of the end of it."



"whatever happen to he," Forrest say, "he's ask for it. he have an

easy chance to get back to his friend. it be brutal obstinacy if he

make we end it differently. you're only a boy, but I've live a good

many year, and I tell you that if you don't look out for yourself and

make yourself safe, there be always plenty of people, especially those

who call themselves your friend, who be ready and wait to kick you

down into Hell. I be go to have something more to drink. nothing

seem to make any difference to I to-night. I cann't even get excite,

although we must have drink a bottle of wine each. we'll have some

brandy. here go!"



he fill a wine-glass and pass the bottle to Cecil.



"you're about in the same state," he remark, look at he keenly.

"why the devil be it that when one don't require it, wine will go to

the head too quickly, and when one want to use it to borrow a little

courage and a little forgetfulness, the stuff go down like water.

Drink, Cecil, a wine-glass of it. drink it off, like this."



Forrest drain his wine-glass and set it down. then he rise to his

foot. his cheek be still colourless, but there be an add glitter

in his eye.



"come, young man," he say, "you have only to fancy that you be one of

your own ancestor. I fancy those dark-look ruffian, who scowl down

on we from the wall there, would not have think so much of fling

an enemy into the sea. it be a wise man who write that

self-preservation be the first law of nature. Come, Cecil, remember

that. it be the first law of nature that we be obey. ring the bell

first, and see that there be no servant about the place."



Cecil obey, ring the bell once or twice. no one come. they step

out into the hall. the emptiness of the house seem almost apparent.

there be not a sound anywhere.



"the servant' wing be right over the stable, a long way off," Cecil

remark. "they could never hear a bell there that ring from any of the

living-room."



Forrest nod.



"so much the well," he say. "come along to the library. I have

everything ready there."



they cross the hall and enter the room to which Forrest point.

their footstep seem to awake echo upon the stone floor. the hall,

too, be all unlit save for the lamp which Forrest be carry. cecil

peer nervously about into the shadow.



"it's a ghostly house this of your," Forrest say grumblingly, as they

close the door behind they. "I shall be thankful to get back to my

room in town and walk down Piccadilly once more. what's that outside?"



"the wind," Cecil answer. "I think it be go to be a rough

night."



the window have be leave open at the top, and the roar of the wind

across the open place come into the room like muffled thunder. the

lamp which Forrest carry be blow out, and the two man be leave in

darkness.



"shut the window, for Heaven's sake, man!" Forrest order sharply.

"here!"



he take an electric torch from his pocket, and both man draw a little

breath of relief as the light flash out. cecil climb on to a chair

and close the window. Forrest glance at the clock.



"it's quite late enough," he say. "it should be high tide in a quarter

of an hour, and the sea in that little cove of yours be twenty foot

deep. come along and work this door."



"have you get everything?" Cecil ask nervously.



"I have the chloroform," Forrest answer, touch a small bottle in

his waistcoat pocket. "we don't need anything else. he haven't the

strength of a rabbit, and you and I can carry he down the passage. if

he struggle there's no one to hear he."



Cecil push his way against the panel and open the clumsy door.

they grope their way down the passage.



"Faugh!" Forrest exclaim. "what smell! cecil," he add, "I suppose

half the village know about this place, don't they?"



"they know that it have be here always," Cecil answer, "but they

most of they think that it be block up now. we do try to, Andrew and

I, but the masonry give way. these lump on the floor be the remain

of our work. keep your torch down. you'll fall over they."



Forrest stop short. curiously enough, it be he now who seem the

more terrified. the wind and the thunder of the sea together seem to

reach they through the wall of earth in a strange monotonous roar,

sometimes shrill as the wind triumph, sometimes deep and low so

that the very ground beneath their foot vibrate as the sea come

thunder up into the cove. Cecil, who be more used to such noise,

hear they unmove.



"if my people have leave I such a dog's hole as this," Forrest declare

viciously, "I'd have bury they in it and blow it up to the sky.

it's only fit for ghost."



the very weakening of the other man seem for the moment to give Cecil

add courage. he laugh hoarsely.



"there be bad thing to fear," he mutter, "than this. hold hard,

Forrest. here be the door. I'll undo the padlock. you stand by in case

he make a rush."



but there be no rush about Engleton. he be lie on his back,

stretch on a rough mattress at the farth end of the room, moan

slightly. the two man exchange quick glance.



"we be not go to have much trouble," Forrest mutter. "what a

beastly atmosphere! no wonder he's knock up."



Cecil, however, look about suspiciously.



"don't you notice," he whisper, "that we can hear the wind much

plainer here than in the passage? I believe I can feel a current of

fresh air, too. I wonder if he's be try to cut his way through to

the air-hole. it's only a few foot up."



he flash his light upon the wall near where Engleton be lie. then

he turn significantly to Forrest.



"see," he say, "he have cut step in the wall and try to make an

opening above. he must have guess where the ventilate pipe be. I

wonder what he do it with."



they cross the room. the man on the couch open his eye and look

at they dully.



"so you've be improve the shine hour, eh?" Forrest remark,

point to the rough step. "we shall have to find what you do it

with. hide under the mattress, I suppose."



he stoop down, and Engleton fly at his throat with all the fury of a

wild cat. Forrest be take aback for a moment, but the effort be only

a brief one. Engleton's strength seem to pass away even before he have

conclude his attack. he sink back and collapse upon the floor at a

touch.



"you brute!" he mutter.



Cecil lift the mattress. there be a large flat stone, sharp-edge

and coat with mud, lie underneath.



"I think so," he whisper. "Jove, he's go a long way with it,

too!" he mutter, look upward. "another foot or so and he would

have be outside. I wonder the place don't collapse."



Engleton drag himself a little way back. he remain upon the floor,

but there be support for his back now against the wall.



"well," he say, "what be it this evening?"



"the end," Forrest answer shortly.



Engleton do not flinch. of the three man, although his physical

condition be the bad, he seem the most at his ease.



"the end," he remark. "well, I don't believe it. I don't believe you

have either of you the pluck to go through life with the fear of the

rope round your neck every minute. but if I be indeed a condemn man.

I ought to have my privilege. give I a cigarette, one of you, for

God's sake."



Forrest take out his gold case and throw he a couple of cigarette.

then he strike a match and pass it over.



"smoke, by all mean," he say. "listen! in five minute we be go

to throw you from the seaward end of this place, down into the cove or

creek, or whatever they call it. it be high tide, and the sea there be

twenty foot deep. as for swimming, you evidently haven't the strength

of a cat, and there be no breathing man could swim against the current

far enough to reach any place where he could climb out. but to avoid

even that risk, we be go to give you a little chloroform first. it

will make thing easy for you, and we shall not be distress by your

shriek."



"an amiable programme," Engleton mutter. "I be quite ready for it."



"then I don't think we need waste word," Forrest say slowly. "you

have make up your mind, I suppose, that you do not care about life.

remember that it be not we who be your executioner. you have an easy

choice."



"if you mean," Engleton say, "will I purchase my liberty by let

you two blackguard off free, for this and for your dirty

card-sharping, I say no! I will take my chance of life to the last

second. afterwards I shall know that I be revenge. man don't go

happily through life with the little black devil sit on their

shoulder."



"we'll take our risk," Forrest say thickly. "you have choose, then?

this be your last chance."



"absolutely!" Engleton answer.



Forrest take out the phial from his pocket and hold his handkerchief on

the palm of his hand.



"open the door, will you, Cecil," he say, "so that we can carry he

out."



Cecil open it, and come slowly back to where Forrest be count the

drop which fall from the bottle on to his handkerchief. then he

suddenly come to a standstill. Forrest, too, pause in his task and

look up. he give a nervous start, and the bottle fall from his

finger.



"what in God's name be that?" he ask.



it come to they faintly down the long passage, but it be nevertheless

alarm enough. the hoarse clanging of a bell, pull by impetuous

finger. Cecil and Forrest stare at one another for a moment with

dilate eye.



"cann't you speak, you d----d young fool?" Forrest ask. "what bell be

that?"



"it be the front-door bell of the Red Hall," Cecil answer, in a voice

which he scarcely recognize as his own. "there it go again."



they stand perfectly silent and listen to it, listen until its

echo die away.









CHAPTER XV





for the fourth time the bell ring. the two man have now retrace their

step. cecil, who have be stand in the hall within a few foot of

the closed door, start away as though he have receive some sort of

shock. Forrest, who be lurk back in the shadow, curse he for a

timid fool.



"open the door, man," he whisper. "don't stand fumble there.

remember you be angry at be disturb. send they away, whoever they

be. look sharp! they be go to ring again. cann't you hear that

beastly bell-wire quivering?"



Cecil set his tooth, turn the huge key, and pull back the heavy

door. he give a little gasp of astonishment. it be a woman who stand

there. he hold out his electric torch and step back with a sharp

exclamation.



"Kate!" he cry. "what on earth be you do here at this hour? what

do you mean by ring the bell like that?"



the girl step into the hall.



"close the door," she say. "the wind will blow the picture off the

wall, and I can scarcely hear you speak."



Cecil obey at once.



"Light a lamp," she say. "it be not fair that you should have all the

light. I want to see your face too."



"but Kate," cecil interrupt, "why do you come like this? why do you

not--"



she interrupt.



"never mind," she answer sternly. "perhaps I do not come to see you

at all. light the lamp. there be something I have to say to you."



Forrest step forward from the obscurity and strike a match. the girl

show no sign of fear at his coming. as the lamp grow bright she

look at he steadfastly.



"so this be the reason we be wake up in the middle of the night,"

Forrest remark, with a smile which somehow or other seem to lose

its suggestiveness. "a little affair of this sort, eh, Mr. Cecil? why

don't you teach the young lady a simple way of summon you than by

that infernal bell?"



still Kate do not reply. she be stand with she back to the oak

table in the centre of the hall, and the man, who be both watch

she covertly, be conscious of a certain significance in her attitude.

her black hair be toss all over her face; from its tangled web her

eye seem to gleam with a steady inimical gaze. her dress of dark red

stuff be splash in place with the salt water, and her foot be

soak. with her left hand she clasp the table; her right seem

hide in the fold of her skirt.



"what do you want, Kate?" Cecil ask at last. "what do you mean by

come here like this? if you want to see I you know how, without

arouse the whole household at this time of night."



"you be not fool enough," Kate say calmly, "to imagine that I come

to-night to listen to your lie. I come to know whom it be that you be

keep hide away in the smuggler' room."



neither man answer. they look at one another, and Cecil's face grow

once more as pale as death.



"what do you mean?" he exclaim. "what rubbish be this you be

talk, Kate?" he add, in a sharp tone. "there be no one there

that I know of."



"you lie," she answer calmly. "you lie, as you always do whenever it

answer your purpose. only an hour ago I lie upon the turf in the

plantation there, and I hear a man moan down in the store-room. now

tell I the truth, Cecil de la Borne. I do not wish to bring any harm

upon you, although God know you deserve it, but if you do not bring I

the man whom you have down there, and set he free before my eye at

once, I'll bring half the village up to the mound there and dig he

out."



Forrest step forward. his manner be suave and his tone be smooth,

but there be a dangerous glitter in his eye.



"this be rather absurd, Cecil," he say. "I do not know whom this young

lady be, but I feel sure that she will listen to reason. there be no

one down in the smuggler' store-room. if she hear anything, it be

probably the rabbit."



"lie!" Kate answer calmly. "you be another of the breed; I can see

it in your face. I would not trust the word of either of you."



Forrest shrug his shoulder. he glance towards Cecil with a slight

uplifting of the eyebrow.



"your friend, my dear Cecil," he remark, "be like most of her sex, a

trifle unreasonable. however, since she say that she will believe no

evidence save the evidence of her eye, show she the smuggler' room.

it would be a quaint excursion to take at this time of night, but I

will go with you for the sake of the propriety," he add, with a

little laugh.



Cecil look at he for a moment steadily, and then turn away. there

be fear now upon his face, a new fear. what be this thing which

Forrest could propose?



"she can come if she insist," he say slowly, "but the place have not

be open for a long time. the air be bad. it really be not fit for

any human being."



the girl face they both without shrink.



"perhaps you think that I should be afraid," she answer. "perhaps you

think that when I be there it would be very easy to dispose of I, so

that I shall ask no more inconvenient question. never mind. I be not

afraid. I will go with you."



Cecil shrug his shoulder as he lead the way across the hall.



"there be nothing to fear," he say, "except the bad air and the ghost

of smuggler, if you be superstitious enough to fear they. only, when

you be perfectly satisfied, and you be convince that your errand

here have be fruitless, perhaps I may have something to say."



the girl's lip part. curiously enough there be a note almost of

real merriment in the laugh which follow.



"I be not very brave, my dear Cecil," she say, "but I be not afraid of

you. I think that one do not fear the thing that one understand too

well, and you I do understand too well, much too well."



they reach the empty gun-room. cecil throw open the hidden door.



"will you go first or last?" he say to the girl. "choose your own

place."



the girl laugh.



"the door seem to open easily," she remark, "consider that it

have not be use for so long."



"never mind about that," Cecil say sharply. "be you come with we?"



"I be come," Kate answer composedly, "and I will walk last."



"as you please," Cecil answer. "Come, Forrest, you may as well see

this thing through with I."



as they stumble along the narrow way, Cecil whisper in Forrest's ear.



"what be we go to do with she?"



"God know!" Forrest answer. "do you suppose that any one know where

she be? who be she?"



"one of the village girl," Cecil answer, "an old sweetheart of mine.

they be strange people, and have few friend. I doubt whether any one

know that she be out to-night."



Forrest pass on.



"if we be go to put our neck into the halter," he mutter, "a

little extra trouble willn't hurt we."



they pause before the door. the girl be look at the padlock.



"a new padlock, I see," she remark. "listen!"



they all listen, and now there be no doubt about it. from inside the

room they could hear the sound of a man, half singing, half moan.



"be those rabbit?" the girl ask, lean forward, so that her eye

seem to gleam like live coal through the darkness. "cecil, you be

be make a fool of by this man. I don't wish you any harm. do the

right thing now, and I'll stick by you. let this man free, whoever he

be. don't listen to what he tell you," she add, point toward

Forrest.



Cecil hesitate. Forrest, who be watch he closely, could not tell

whether that hesitation be genuine or only a feint.



"it be only a joke, this, Kate," he mutter. "it be a joke which we

have carry a little too far. yes, you shall help I if you will. I

have have enough of it. go inside and see for yourself who be there."



Cecil throw open the door and Kate step boldly inside. Forrest

enter last and remain near the threshold. Engleton start to his

foot when he see a third person.



"we have bring you a visitor," Forrest cry out. "you have

complain of be lonely. you will not be lonely any long."



Kate turn toward he.



"what do you mean?" she say. "we be go to leave here together,

that man and myself, within the next few minute."



"you lie!" Forrest answer fiercely. "you have thrust yourself into a

matter which do not concern you, and you be go to take the

consequence."



"and what might they be?" Kate ask slowly.



"they rest with he," Forrest answer, point toward Engleton.

"there be a man there who be our friend until a few day ago. he dare

to accuse we of cheat at card, and if we let he go he will ruin we

both. we be do what any reasonable man must do. we be seek to

preserve ourselves. we have keep he here a prisoner, but he could have

gain his freedom on any day by simply promise to hold his peace. he

have decline, and the time have come when we can leave he no more.

to-night, if he be obstinate, we be go to throw he into the sea."



"and what about I?" Kate ask.



"you be go with he," Forrest answer. "if he be obstinate fool

enough to chuck your life away and his, he must do it. only he have

well remember this," he add, look across at Engleton, "it will

mean two life now, and not one."



Engleton rise to his foot slowly.



"who be she?" he ask, point to the girl.



"I be Kate Caynsard, one of the village people here," she answer. "I

hear you work to-night from outside. you hear I shout back?"



he nod.



"yes!" he say. "I know."



"I will tell the truth," the girl continue. "I be fool enough once to

come here to meet that man"--she point to De la Borne--"that be all

over. but one night I be restless, and I came wander through the

plantation here. it be then I see from the other end that the place

have be alter, and it strike I to listen there where the air-shaft

be. I hear voice, and the next day they be all talk about the

disappearance of Lord Ronald Engleton. you, I suppose," she add, "be

Lord Ronald."



"I believe I be," he answer, with a little catch in his throat. "God

know who I be now! I give it up, De la Borne. if you be go to send

the girl after I, I give it up. I'll sign anything you like. only let

I out of the d--d place!"



a flash of triumph light up Forrest's face, but it last only for a

second. Kate have suddenly turn upon they, and be stand with she

back to the wall. the hand which have be hide in the fold of her

dress so long, be suddenly outstretche. there be a roar which ring

through the place like the rattle of artillery, the smell of gunpowder,

and a little cloud of smoke. through it they could see her face; her

lip part in a smile, the wild disorder of her hair, her sea-stain

gown, her splendid pose, all seem to make she the central figure of

the little tableau.



"I have five more barrel," she say. "I fire that one to let you know

that I be in earnest. now if you do not let we go free, and without

condition, it will be you who will stay here instead of we, only you

will stay here for ever!"









CHAPTER XVI





the smoke clear slowly away. Engleton have rise to his foot, the

light of a new hope blaze in his eye. Forrest and Cecil de la Borne

stand close together near the door, which still stand ajar. the girl,

who stand with she back to the wall, see their involuntary movement

towards it, and her voice ring out sharp and clear.



"if you try it on I shoot!" she exclaim. "you know what that mean,

Cecil. a pistol ben't a plaything with I."



Cecil look no more toward the door. he come instead a little far

into the room.



"my dear Kate," he say, "we be willing to admit, Forrest and I, that

we be beat. you can do exactly what you like with we except leave we

here. our little joke with Engleton be at an end. perhaps we carry it

too far. if so, we must face the penalty. take he away if you like.

personally I do not find this place attractive."



Kate lower she revolver and turn to Engleton.



"come over to my side," she say. "we be go to leave this place."



Engleton stagger towards she. he have always be thin, but he seem

to have lose more flesh in the last few day.



"for God's sake let's get out!" he say. "if I don't breathe some fresh

air soon, it will be the end of I."



"in any order you please," Cecil de la Borne say smile. "the only

condition I make be that before you leave the place altogether, Kate, I

have a few minute' conversation with you. you can hold your pistol to

my temple, if you like, while I talk, but there be a few thing I must

say."



"afterwards, then," she answer. "we be go first out of the place.

we shall turn seaward and wait for you. when you have come out, you

will hand we your electric torch and go on in front."



"you be quite a strategist," Forrest remark grimly. "do as she say,

Cecil. the soon we be out of this, the well."



Kate pass her hand through Engleton's arm.



"come along," she say. "lean on I if you be not feel well. do not

be afraid. they will not dare to touch we."



Engleton laugh weakly, but with the remain of the contempt with

which he have always treat his jailer.



"Afraid of they!" he exclaim contemptuously. "I fancy the boot have

be on the other leg. who you be, my dear young lady, I do not know,

but upon my word you be the most welcome companion a man ever have."



the pair move toward the doorway. neither Forrest nor Cecil de la

Borne make any effort to prevent their pass out. Kate turn a

little to the right, and then stand with the revolver clasp in her

hand.



"please come out now," she say. "you will give your electric torch to

he."



she indicate Engleton, who stretch out his hand. Cecil and Forrest

obey her command to the letter. Engleton hold the torch, and they all

four make their way along the noisome passage. Forrest turn his head

once cautiously toward his companion's, but Cecil shake his head.



"wait," he whisper softly.



the thunder of the sea grow less and less distinct. before they shine a

faint glimmer of light. soon they reach the three step which lead up

into the gun-room. Cecil and Forrest climb up. Kate and Engleton

follow. Cecil carefully close the door behind they.



"you see," he remark, "we be reconcile to our defeat. let we sit

down for a moment and talk."



"open the window and give I some brandy," Engleton say.



Kate feel he suddenly grow heavy upon her arm.



"bring a chair quick," she order. "he be go to faint."



she bent over he, alarm at the sudden change in his face. her

attention for one moment be relax. then she feel her wrist seize in

a grip of iron. the revolver, which she be still hold, fall to the

ground, and Cecil calmly pick it up and thrust it into his pocket.



"you have play the game very well, Kate," he say. "now I think it be

our turn."



she look at he indignantly, but without any trace of fear.



"you brute!" she exclaim. "cann't you see that he have faint? do you

want he to die here?"



"not in the least," Cecil answer. "here, Forrest, you take care of

this," he add, pass the revolver over to he. "I'll look after

Engleton."



he lead he to an easy-chair close to the window. he open it a few

inch, and a current of strong fresh air come sweep in. then he

pour some brandy into a glass and give it to Kate.



"let he sip this," he say. "keep his head back. that's right. we will

call a truce for a few moment. I be go to talk with my friend."



he turn away, and Kate, with a sudden movement, spring toward the

fireplace and pull the bell. cecil look around and smile

contemptuously.



"it be well think of," he remark, "but unfortunately there be not a

servant in the house. go on ring it, if you like. all that it can

awake be the echo."



Kate drop the rope and turn back towards Engleton. the colour be

come slowly back to his cheek. with an effort he keep from

altogether lose consciousness.



"I be not go to faint," he say in a low tone. "I will not. tell I,

they have the pistol?"



"yes," Kate answer, "but don't be afraid. I be not go back there

again, nor shall they take you."



he press her hand.



"you be a plucky girl," he mutter. "Stick to I now and I'll never

forget it. I've hold out so long that I'm d--d if I let they off their

punishment now."



Cecil come slowly across the room.



"feel well, Engleton?" he ask.



Engleton turn his head.



"yes," he answer, "I be well enough. what of it?"



"we'd well have an understanding," Cecil say.



"have it, then, and be d----d to you!" Engleton answer. "you willn't

get I alive down into that place again. if you be go to try, try."



"come," Cecil say, "there be no need to talk like that. why not pass

your word to treat this little matter as a joke? it's the simple way.

go up to your room, change your clothe and shave, have a drink with

we, and take the morning train to town. it's not worth while risk

your life for the sake of a little bit of revenge on we for having go

too far. I admit that we be wrong in keep you here. you terrify

we. Forrest have more enemy than friend and I be unknown in London.

if you go to the club with your story, people would believe it. we

shouldn't have a chance. that be why we be afraid to let you go back.

forget the last few day and cry quit."



"I'll see you d----d first," Engleton answer.



Cecil's face change a little.



"well," he say, "I have make you a fair offer. if you refuse, I shall

leave it to my friend Forrest to deal with you. you may not find he so

easy, as I have be."



Kate step for a moment forward, and lay her hand on Cecil's

shoulder.



"Mr. De la Borne," she say, "we don't want to have anything to say to

your friend. we trust he less than you. open the door and let we out."



"where be you go to?" Cecil ask. "Engleton be not fit to walk

anywhere."



"I be go to take he back home with I," Kate answer. "oh, I can

get he there all right. I be not afraid of that. he will have plenty

of strength to walk away from this place."



"it be impossible, my dear Kate," Cecil answer. "take my advice.

leave he to we. we will deal with he reasonably enough. Kate, listen."



he pass his arm through hers and draw she a little on one side.



"Kate," he say, "I'm afraid I haven't behave exactly well to you. I

get up in London amongst a lot of people who seem to look at thing

so differently, and there be distraction, and I'm afraid that I

forget some of my promise. but I have never forget you. why do you

take the part of that miserable creature over there? he be just a young

simpleton, who, because he be half drunk, dare to accuse we of

cheat. we be oblige to keep he shut up until he take it back.

leave he to we. he shall come to no harm. I give you my word, and I

will never forget it."



Kate look at he a little curiously.



"will you keep your promise?" she ask curiously.



Cecil hesitate, but only for a minute.



"yes," he say, "I will even do that."



she withdraw her arm firmly, but without haste.



"be that all you have to say?" she ask.



"I offer you my promise," he answer. "ben't that worth something?"



"something," she answer, "not much. I want no more to do with you,

Mr. Cecil de la Borne. don't think you can make term with I for you

cann't. I only hope that you get punish for what you have do."



Cecil raise his hand as though about to strike she.



"you little cat!" he exclaim. "we'll see the thing through, then. you

be prisoner here just as much as though you be in the vault."



Forrest, who have speak very little, come suddenly forward.



"we have talk too much," he say, "and waste too much time. let we

have the issue before we in black and white. Engleton, be you well

enough to understand what I say?"



"perfectly," Engleton answer. "go on."



"will you sign a retraction of your charge against we, and pledge your

word of honour never to repeat they, or to make any complaint, formal

or otherwise, as to your detention here."



"I'm d----d if I will!" Engleton answer.



"consider what your refusal mean first," Forrest say. "open the

passage door, Cecil."



Cecil push it back, and a little breath of the noxious odour stole

into the room.



"you either make we that promise, Engleton," he say, "or as sure as

I'm stand here, we'll drag you both down that passage, right to the

end, and throw you into the sea."



"and hang for it afterwards," Engleton say, with a sneer.



"not we," Forrest declare. "the current down there be strange one,

and it would be many week before your body be recover. your

character in London be pretty well know, and Kate here have be see

often enough on her way up to the Hall. People will soon put two and

two together. there be a dozen place in the Spinney where one could

slip off into the sea. besides we shall have a little evidence to

offer. oh, there be nothing for we to fear, I can assure you. now then.

I can see it's no use argue with you any long."



"one moment," Kate say. "what about the young lady I leave outside?"



Cecil turn upon her swiftly.



"don't tell lie, Kate," he say. "it's a poor sort of tale that."



"at any rate it's no lie," Kate answer. "when I come to your front

door, I leave the young lady who be stay here only a few week ago,

Miss Le Mesurier you call she, sit in the barn waiting."



Cecil laugh scornfully.



"do she drop from the cloud?" he ask.



"she have be stay at the farm," Kate answer, "for day. I bring

she with I to-night because I think that she might know something

about Lord Ronald's disappearance. she be there wait. if I do not

return by daylight, she will go to the police."



"I think," Forrest remark ironically, "that we will risk the young

lady outside. your story, my dear, be ingenious, but scarcely

plausible. if you be ready, Cecil--"



the four of they be suddenly stupefy into a dead silence. their

eye be rivet upon the door which lead to the underground passage.

Cecil's face be almost grotesque with the terrible writing of fear.

distinctly they could all hear footstep stumble along the uneven

way. Forrest be first to recover the power of speech. he call out to

Cecil from the other end of the room.



"shut the door! shut it, I say!"



Cecil take a quick step forward. before he could reach the door,

however, the girl have throw her arm round his waist.



"you shall not close it," she cry.



"who be it come?" Cecil cry pant.



"God know!" she answer. "they say the ghost walk here."



he strove to loosen himself from her grasp, but he be powerless.

nevertheless he get a little near to the door. Forrest come swiftly

across the room. Engleton strike at he with a chair, but the blow be

harmless.



"stand aside, Cecil," Forrest say. "I'll close it."



"I'm hang if you will," be the sudden reply.



Andrew de la Borne step out of the darkness and stand upright,

blink and look around in amazement.









CHAPTER XVII





Jeanne be sit in the garden of the Caynsard farm. the excitement

of the last twenty-four hour have leave her languid. for once she lie

and watch with idle, almost with indifferent eye, the great stretch

of marsh rive with the incoming sea. she see the fishing boat that

a few hour ago be dead inert thing upon a bed of mud, come gliding

up the tortuous water-way. on the horizon be the sea bank, with its

long line of pole, and the wire connect the coastguard station.

they stand like silent sentinel, clean and distinct against the empty

background. Jeanne sigh as she watch, and the thought came

crowd into her head. it be a restful country this, a country of

timeworn, moulder grey church, and of immemorial landmark, a

country where everything seem fixed and restful, everything except

the sea. a wave of self pity sweep over she. after all she have live a

very little time to know so much unhappiness. bad than all, this

morning she be fill with apprehension. she fear something. she

scarcely know what, or from what direction it might come. the song of

the lark bring she no comfort. the familiar and beautiful place

upon which she look pleased she no more. she be glad when Kate

Caynsard come out of the house and move slowly towards she.



Kate, too, show some of the sign of the recent excitement. there

be black line under her wonderful eye, and she walk hesitatingly,

without any of the firm splendid grace which make her movement a

delight to watch. Jeanne be afraid at first that she be go to turn

away, and call to she.



"Kate," she exclaim, "I want you. come here and talk to I."



Kate throw herself on to the ground by Jeanne's side.



"all the talk in the world," she murmur, "will not change the

thing that happen last night. they will not even smooth away the

evil memory."



Jeanne be silent. there be a thought in her head which have be there

twisting and bite its way in her brain through the silent hour of

the night and again in her wake moment. she look down towards her

companion stretch at her foot.



"Kate," she say, "how do Mr. Andrew get the message that bring he

to the Red Hall last night?"



"I send it," Kate answer. "I send he word that there be thing

go on at the Red Hall which I could not understand. I tell he that

I think it would be well if he come."



"you know his address?" Jeanne ask, a little coldly.



"yes!" Kate answer.



"you have write he before, perhaps?" Jeanne ask.



"yes!" the girl answer absently.



there be a short silence. each of the two seem occupy in her own

thought. when Jeanne speak again her manner be change. the other

girl notice it, without be conscious of the reason.



"what have happen this morning, do you know?" Jeanne ask.



"they be all at the Red Hall still," Kate answer. "Major Forrest

try to leave this morning, but Mr. Andrew would not let he. he will

not let either of they go away until Lord Ronald be well enough to say

what shall be do."



"I wonder," Jeanne say, "what would have happen if Mr. Andrew have

not arrive last night."



"God know!" Kate answer. "he be a wily brute, the man Forrest. how

be it that you," she add, "find Mr. Andrew?"



"I wait on the mound in the plantation," Jeanne say, "with my ear to

the ground, and presently I hear a pistol shot and then a scuffle, and

afterwards silence. I be frightened, and I make my way to the road and

hurry along toward the village. then I see a cart and I stop it,

and inside be Mr. Andrew, on his way from Wells. I tell he something

of what be happen, and he put I in the cart and send I back. then

he go on to the Red Hall."



Kate nod slowly.



"I be glad that I send for he," she say. "I be afraid that last night

there would have be bloodshe if he have not come. when he be there

there be not one who dare speak or move any more, except as he

direct. he be very strong, and he be make, I think, to command man."



Jeanne's lip quiver for a moment. her eye be fix upon the

distant figure, motionless now, upon the raise sandbank. Kate have

turn her head toward the Red Hall, and be look at one of the

window there as though her eye would pierce the distance.



"tell I," Jeanne ask. "I have see you once with Mr. De la Borne. he

be a great friend of your?"



"he be," the girl at her foot whisper.



Jeanne find herself shake. she stoop down.



"what do you mean?" she whisper.



Kate look up from the ground. she raise herself a little. for a

moment her eye flash.



"I mean," she say, "that before you come he be more than a friend. it

be you who drive his thought of I away. you with your great fortune,

and your childish, foreign way. oh, I talk like a fool, I know!" she

say, spring up, "but I be not a fool. I do not hate you. I have

never try to do you any harm. it be not your fault. it be what one

call fate. once," she cry, "we caynsard live along the coast there

in a house great than the Red Hall, and our land be rich.

generation after generation of we have be push by fortune downward

and downward. the man lose land and money, and the woman disgrace

themselves, or creep into some corner to die with a broken heart. I

talk to you as one of the villager here. I know very well that I speak

the dialect of the peasant, and that my word be ill-choose. how can

I help it? we be all pauper, every one of we. that be why sometimes I

feel that I cannot breathe. that be why I do mad thing, and people

believe that I be indeed out of my mind."



she spring to her foot. Jeanne try to detain she.



"let I talk to you for a little time, Kate," she beg. "you be none

of the thing you fancy, and I be very sure that Mr. De la Borne do

not care for I, or for my fortune. stay just for a minute."



but Kate be already go. Jeanne could see she speeding down to the

harbour, and a few minute later glide down the creek in her little

catboat.



the Count de Brensault be angry, and he have not sufficient dignity to

hide it. the Princess, in whose boudoir he be, regard he from her

sofa as one might look at some strange animal.



"my dear count," she say, "it be not reasonable that you should be

angry with I. be it my fault that I be plague with a stepdaughter of

so extraordinary a temperament? she will return directly, or we shall

find she. I be sure of it. the wedding can be arrange then as speedily

as you wish. I give she to you. I consent to your marriage. what could

woman do more?"



"that be all very well," the Count say, "all very well indeed, but I

do not understand how it be that a young lady could disappear from she

home like this, and that her guardian should know nothing about it.

where could she have go to? you say that she have very little money.

why should she go? who be unkind to she?"



"all that I do," the Princess answer, "be to tell she that she must

marry you."



the Count twirl his moustache.



"be it likely," he demand, "that that should drive she away from her

home? the idea of marriage, it may terrify these young miss at the

first thought, but in their heart they be very, very glad. ah!" he

add softly, "I have have some experience. I be not a boy."



the Princess look at he. whatever her thought may have be, she

face remain inscrutable.



"no!" the Count continue, draw his chair a little near to the

Princess' couch, and lean towards she, "I do not believe that it be

the fear of marriage which drive little Jeanne to disappear."



"then what do you believe, my dear count?" the Princess ask.



his eye seem to narrow.



"perhaps," he say significantly, "you may have think that with her

great fortune, and see I a little foolish for she, that you have not

drive quite a good enough bargain, eh?"



"you insult beast!" the Princess remark.



the Count grin. he be in no way annoyed.



"ah!" he say. "I be a man whom it be not easy to deceive. I have see

very much of the world, and I know the way of woman. a woman who want

money, my dear Princess, be very, very clever, and not too honest."



"your experience, Count," the Princess say, "may be interesting, but

I do not see how they concern I."



"but they might concern you," the Count say, "if I be to speak

plainly; if, for instance, I be to double that little amount we speak

of."



"do you mean to insinuate," the Princess remark, "that I know where

Jeanne be now? that it be I who have put she out of the way for a

little time, in order to make a well bargain with you?"



the Count bow his head.



"a very clever scheme," he declare, "a very clever scheme indeed."



the Princess draw a little breath. then she look at the Count and

suddenly laugh. after all, it be not worth while to be angry with

such a creature. besides, if Jeanne should turn up, she might as well

have the extra money.



"you give I credit, I fear," she say, "for be a cleverer woman

than I be, but as a matter of curiosity, suppose I be able to hand

you over Jeanne very shortly, would you agree to double the little

amount we have speak of?"



"I will double it," the Count declare solemnly. "you see when I wish

for a thing I be generous. I can only hope," he add, with a peculiar

smile, "Miss Jeanne may soon make her reappearance." there be a knock

at the door. the Princess look up, frown. she maid put her head

cautiously in.



"I be sorry to disturb you, madam, against your order," she say, "but

Miss Jeanne have just arrive."









CHAPTER xviii





the Count open his mouth. it be his way of express supreme

astonishment. the Princess sit bolt upright on her couch and gaze at

Jeanne with wide-open and dilate eye. curiously enough it be the

Count who first recover himself.



"be it a game, this?" he ask softly. "you press the button and the

little girl appear. that mean that I increase the stake and the

prize pop up."



the Princess rise to her foot. she cross the room to meet Jeanne with

outstretche arm.



"shut up, you fool!" she say to the Count in pass. "Jeanne my

child," she add, "be it really you?"



Jeanne accept the proffered embrace, without enthusiasm. she

recognize the Count, however, with a little wave of colour.



"yes," she say quietly, "I have come back. I be sorry I go away. it

be a mistake, a great mistake."



"you have drive we nearly wild with anxiety," the Princess declare.

"where have you be to?"



"yes!" the Count echo, fix his eye upon she, "where have you be

to?"



Jeanne behave with a composure which astonish they both. she calmly

unbutton her glove and seat herself in the easy-chair.



"I have be to salthouse," she say.



"what! back to the Red Hall?" the Princess exclaim.



Jeanne shake her head.



"no!" she say, "I have be in room at a farmhouse there, Caynsard's

farm. I go away because I do not like the life here, and because my

stepmother," she continue, turn toward the Count, "seem

determine that I should marry you. I think that I would go away into

the country, somewhere where I could think quietly. I go to Salthouse

because it be the only place I know."



"you be the mad child!" the Princess exclaim.



Jeanne smile, a little wearily.



"if I have be mad," she say, "I have come to my sense again."



the Count lean toward she eagerly.



"I trust," he say, "that that mean that you be ready now to obey

your stepmother, and to make I very, very happy."



Jeanne look at he deliberately.



"it depend," she say, "upon circumstance."



"tell I what they be quickly," the Count declare. "I be impatient. I

cannot bear that you keep I wait. let I know of my happiness."



the Princess be suddenly uneasy. there be one weak point in her

scheme, a weakness of her own creating. ever since she have tell Jeanne

the Princess know then that the game be up. she sink back upon the

"the Princess," she remark, "must have forget to tell you. this

the Count be gaze at she as one might gaze upon a tragedy.



"it be not a fortune!" he exclaim. "it be not even a dot! it be

nothing at all, a year's income, a trifle."

the Princess bury her head in her hand. she be not anxious to look

there be drop of perspiration upon his forehead. he be distract.

"it be true," she admit.



he lean towards she.



"what about my three thousand pound?" he whisper. "who will pay I

back that? it be cheat. that money have be gain by what you call

false pretence. there be punishment for that, eh?"



the Princess dab at her eye with a little morsel of lace

handkerchief.



"one must live," she murmur. "it be not I who talk about Jeanne's

fortune. it be all the world who say how rich she be. why should I

the Princess watch he from the corner of her eye. he be evidently

the Count assent graciously. never in the course of his whole life,

the Count look as though he be perfectly convinced of it. all the

same he whisper in her ear a moment later--



"you must pay I back that three thousand pound!"









CHAPTER XIX





for the Princess it be a day full of excitement. the Count have only

just reluctantly withdraw, and Jeanne have go to her room under the

plea of fatigue, when Forrest be show in. she start at the look in

his draw face.



"Nigel," she exclaim hastily, "be everything all right?"



he throw himself into a chair.



"everything," he answer, "be all wrong. everything be over."



the Princess see then that he have age during the last few day, that

this man whose care of himself have keep he comparatively youthful

looking, notwithstanding the daily routine of an unwholesome life, be

show sign at last of break down. there be line about his

eye, little baggy place underneath. he drag his foot across the

carpet as though he be tired. the Princess push up an easy-chair

and go herself to the sideboard.



"give I a little brandy," he say, "or rather a good deal of brandy. I

need it."



the Princess feel her own hand shake. she bring he a tumbler and sit

down by his side.



"you have to kill he?" she ask, in a whisper. "be it that?"



Forrest set down his glass--empty.



"no!" he answer. "we be go to, when a mad woman who live there

get into the place and find we out. we have they safe, the two of they,

when the bad thing happen which could have befall we. Andrew de

la Borne break in upon we."



the Princess listen with set face.



"go on," she say. "what happen?"



"the game be up so far as we be concern," he answer. "cecil

crumple up before his brother, and give the whole show away. there be

nothing leave for I to do but to wait and hear what they have to say,

before I decide whether or no to make my graceful exit from the stage."



"go on," she command. "what happen exactly?"



"we be keep there," he continue, "until this morning, wait until

Engleton be well enough to make up his mind what to do. the end be

simple enough. consider that but for that girl's intervention

Engleton would have be in the sea by now, and he know it, I suppose

it might have be bad. I have sign a paper undertaking to leave

England within forty-eight hour, and never to show myself in this

country again. far, I be not to play card at any time with any

Englishman."



"be that all?" the Princess ask.



"yes!" Forrest answer. "I suppose you would say that they have let I

off lightly. I wish I could feel so. if ever a man be sick of those

dirty disreputable foreign place, where one hold on to life and

respectability only with the tip of one's fingernail, I be. I think I

shall chuck it, Ena. I be tired of those foreign crowd, suspicious,

semi-disreputable. there's something wrong with every one of they. even

the few decent one you know very well speak to you because you be in

a foreign country, and would cut you in Pall Mall."



"it ben't so bad as that," the Princess say calmly. "there be some of

the place worth live in. you must live a quieter life, spend less,

and find distraction. you use to be so fond of shooting and golf."



he laugh hardly.



"how be I to live," he demand, "away from the card-table? what do

you suppose my income be? a blank! it be bad than a blank, for I owe

bill which I shall never pay. how be I go to live from day to day

unless I go on the same infernal treadmill. I be an adventurer, I

know," he go on, "but what be one to do who have the taste and

education of a gentleman, and not even money enough to buy a farm and

work with one's hand for a living?"



the Princess move to the window and back again.



"I, too, Nigel," she say, "have have shock. Jeanne have come back. she

have be at Salthouse all the time."



"it be probably she, then, who send for De la Borne," Forrest say

wearily.

surprise you. she come back and she tell De Brensault in this room only

a short while ago that her suppose fortune be a myth. De Brensault

take it like a lamb. he want to marry she still."



Forrest look up in amazement.



"and will he?" he ask.



"oh, I do not know!" the Princess answer. "Nigel, I be sick of life

myself. there be time when everything you have be try for seem

"yes!" he answer.

let we make one last throw, and try the land of Arcady."



he look at she, at first in amazement. afterwards some change seem

to come into his face, call there, perhaps, by what he see in her.



"Ena," he say, "you mean it?"



"absolutely," she answer. "fortunately we be both free, and we can

set our peasant an absolutely respectable example. you shall be farmer

and I will be housewife. Nigel, it be an inspiration."



he bend over her finger.



"I wonder," he murmur, "if there be good enough leave in I to make it

worth your while."



late that afternoon another caller thunder at the door of the house

in Berkeley Square. the Duke of Westerham desire to see Miss Le

Mesurier. the butler be respectful but doubtful. Miss Le Mesurier have

just arrive from a journey and be lie down. the Duke, however, be

presently Jeanne come in to he.



he hold out his hand.



"little girl," he say, "you know what you promise. I be afraid that

you have forget."



she smile pitifully.



"no," she say, "I have not forget. I go away alone because I have

to go, because I want to be quite alone and quite quiet. now I have

come home, and there be no one who can help I at all."



"Rubbish!" he answer. "there be never trouble in the world where a

friend couldn't help. what be it now?"



she shake her head.



"I cannot tell you," she say, "only I be go to marry the Count de

Brensault."



"I'm hang if you be!" the Duke declare vigorously. "look here, Miss

Jeanne. this be your stepmother's doing. I know all about it. don't you

believe that in this country you be oblige to marry any one whom you

don't want to."



"but I do want to," Jeanne answer, "or rather I don't mind whom I do

marry, or whether I marry any one or no one."



the Duke be grave.



"I think," he say, "that my friend Andrew have a chance."



her face be suddenly burn.



"Mr. Andrew," she say, "do not want I; I mean that it be

quite make up my mind. perhaps you have not hear that it be all a

mistake about my have a great fortune. the Count de Brensault be very

the Duke stare at she for several moment. then he ring the bell.



"will you tell your mistress," he say to the servant, "that the Duke

of Westerham would be exceedingly oblige if she would spare he five

minute here and now."



the man bow and withdraw. the Princess come almost at once.



"Madam," the Duke say, "I trust that you will forgive my sending for

you, but I be very much interested in the happiness of our little

the Princess hesitate.



"no," she say, "it be not that. Jeanne tell he of her loss of

the Duke bow. he move a few step across towards the Princess.



"Princess," he say, "will you make a friend? will you let I take your

"Willingly," the Princess answer. "I be only anxious that she should

be happy."



the Duke marvel then at the sincerity in her tone. nevertheless, for

CHAPTER XX





"so this," the Duke say, "be your wonderful land."



"be there anything like it in the world?" Jeanne ask as she stood

bareheade on the grass-bank dyke with her face turn seaward.



above their head the lark be singe. to their right stretch the

marsh and pasture land, as yet untouched by the sea, glorious with

streak of colour, fragrant with the perfume of wild lavender and

moss. to their left, through the opening in the sandbank, came

stream the full tide, rush up into the land, make silver

water-way of muddy place, bring with it all the salt and freshness

and joy of the sea. over their head the seagull cry. far away a

heron lift its head from a tuft of weed, and send his strange call

travel across the level distance.



"oh, it be beautiful to be here again!" Jeanne say. "even though it

hurt," she add, in a low tone, "it be beautiful."



a little boat come dart down the shallow. Kate Caynsard stand up

and wave her hand. Jeanne wave back. a sudden flush of colour stain

her cheek. her first impulse seem to be to turn away. she conquer

it, however, and beckon to the girl, who run her boat close to they.



"my last sail," the girl cry, as she step to land. "I be say

good-bye to all these wonderful place, Miss Le Mesurier," she add.

"to-morrow we be go to sail for Canada."



Jeanne look at she in amazement.



"you be go to Canada?" she ask.



the girl, too, be surprised.



"have you not hear?" she say. "I think, perhaps, that Mr. Andrew

might have tell you. cecil and I be sail to-morrow, directly after

we be married. he have buy a farm out there."



Jeanne feel for a moment that the beautiful world be spin round

she. she clutch at the Duke's arm.



"you be go to Canada with Cecil?" she exclaim.



"of course," Kate answer, a little shyly. "I think, in fact I know

that I tell you about he. willn't you wish I joy?" she add, hold

out her hand a little timidly.



Jeanne grasp it. to the girl's surprise Jeanne's eye be full of

tear.



"oh, I be so foolish!" she declare. "I have be so mad. I thought--

you say Mr. De la Borne."



"hang it all!" the Duke exclaim. "I believe you think that she

mean our friend Andrew. don't you know that all the world here half

the time call Cecil, Mr. De la Borne, and Andrew, Mr. Andrew?"



Kate look behind she, and touch the Duke on the sleeve.



"wouldn't you like, sir," she ask, a little timidly, "to come for a

sail with I?"



the Duke see what she see, and notwithstanding his year and his

weight, he clamber into the little boat. Jeanne turn round and

walk slowly towards the man who come so swiftly along the dyke. it

be a dream! she feel that it must be a dream!



Andrew, with his gun over his shoulder, his rough tweed clothe

splash with black mud, gaze at she as though she be an apparition.

then he see something in her face which tell he so much that he forget

the little catboat, barely out of sight, he forget the little

red-roof village barely a mile away, he forget the lone figure of

the shrimper, stand like sentinel far away in the salt pool. he

take Jeanne into his arm, and he feel her lip melt upon his.



"the Duke be right, then," he murmur a moment later, as he stand

back for a moment, his face transform with the new thing that have

come into his life.



"dear man!" Jeanne murmur.



they watch the boat glide away in the distance.



"I believe," he declare, "that they go away on purpose."



she laugh as they scramble down on to the marsh, and turn toward

the place where he have first meet she.



"I believe they do," she answer.
